# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed the comprehensive analysis of the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) gRPC server implementation in Envoy. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I identified **31 C++ source files** across two main implementations:

### 1. **Legacy Implementation** (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/)
- **GrpcStream** template - Low-level gRPC stream management with backoff and rate limiting
- **GrpcMuxImpl** - Legacy subscription multiplexer
- **DeltaSubscriptionState** - Delta-xDS protocol tracking (legacy)
- Legacy subscription factories and implementations

### 2. **Unified Mux Implementation** (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/)
- **GrpcMuxImpl** template - Generic mux for both SotW and Delta variants
- **GrpcMuxDelta** and **GrpcMuxSotw** - Specialized implementations
- **DeltaSubscriptionState** - Delta-xDS with per-resource versioning and incremental updates
- **SotwSubscriptionState** - State-of-the-world protocol tracking
- **BaseSubscriptionState** - Shared ACK/NACK handling logic

### 3. **Core Components**
- **PausableAckQueue** - Manages ACK/NACK ordering with pause/resume
- **UpdateAck** - Carries nonce and error_detail for protocol acks
- **WatchMap** - Tracks resource subscriptions
- **GrpcMuxFailover** - Primary/secondary failover support
- Supporting infrastructure for EDS caching and xDS source tracking

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed file paths, symbols, call chains, and a comprehensive narrative explanation of how these components work together to implement the ADS gRPC server protocol.

with backoff retry logic, rate limiting, and stream establishment/closure. It implements Grpc::AsyncStreamCallbacks and dispatches incoming DiscoveryResponse messages to the mux layer.\\n\\n## Legacy Implementation (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/)\\n\\nThe legacy implementation includes **GrpcMuxImpl** (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc) which manages subscriptions and multiplexes multiple resource types on a single ADS stream. The legacy delta-xDS variant tracks **DeltaSubscriptionState** (delta_subscription_state.h/cc), handling per-resource versioning and incremental updates. The legacy subscription layer (**GrpcSubscriptionImpl**, grpc_subscription_impl.h/cc) provides subscription management with factory patterns (grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc, grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc).\\n\\n## New Unified Mux Implementation (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/)\\n\\nThe newer unified implementation provides template-based generic mux management with:\\n\\n- **GrpcMuxImpl** template (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc) - Generic mux managing subscriptions and request queuing\\n- **GrpcMuxDelta** - Delta-xDS specialization of GrpcMuxImpl\\n- **GrpcMuxSotw** - State-of-the-world (SotW) xDS specialization\\n- **BaseSubscriptionState** template (subscription_state.h) - Base protocol state tracker with ACK/NACK handling via **UpdateAck** struct\\n- **DeltaSubscriptionState** (delta_subscription_state.h/cc) - Tracks delta-xDS protocol state with per-resource version tracking (ResourceState) and incremental updates (names_added_, names_removed_)\\n- **SotwSubscriptionState** (sotw_subscription_state.h/cc) - Tracks state-of-the-world protocol state with full resource set management and version_info tracking\\n- **DeltaSubscriptionStateFactory** and **SotwSubscriptionStateFactory** - Create appropriate subscription state instances\\n\\n## Resource Subscription and ACK/NACK Processing\\n\\nResource subscription tracking is managed through:\\n\\n- **WatchMap** (watch_map.h/cc) - Maps resource name watches to subscription callbacks\\n- **PausableAckQueue** (pausable_ack_queue.h/cc) - Queues ACKs/NACKs with pause/resume capability for ordered delivery\\n- **UpdateAck** struct (update_ack.h) - Carries nonce, type_url, and error_detail for ACK/NACK handling\\n\\nThe ACK/NACK mechanism works by:\\n1. BaseSubscriptionState::handleResponse() copies the response nonce and marks errors in UpdateAck\\n2. getNextRequestWithAck() includes the nonce (ACK) and optional error_detail (NACK) in the next DiscoveryRequest\\n3. handleBadResponse() sets error_detail.code to Internal when validation fails, triggering a NACK\\n\\n## Additional Support Components\\n\\n- **GrpcMuxContext** (grpc_mux_context.h) - Configuration context for mux creation\\n- **GrpcMuxFailover** (grpc_mux_failover.h) - Failover support for primary/secondary xDS sources\\n- **EdsResourcesCacheImpl** (eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc) - Caches EDS resources for optimization\\n- **XdsSourceId** (xds_source_id.h/cc) - Tracks xDS source identification\\n- **NewGrpcMuxImpl** (new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc) - Intermediate mux variant for migration\\n\\nThis architecture separates concerns: the GrpcStream handles transport-level gRPC operations, the mux manages resource subscriptions and request queuing, subscription states track protocol state and ACK/NACK logic, and the watch map manages application-level resource interest callbacks.\"\n}\n",

BaseSubscriptionState::handleResponse() copies the response nonce and marks errors in UpdateAck\\n2. getNextRequestWithAck() includes the nonce (ACK) and optional error_detail (NACK) in the next DiscoveryRequest\\n3. handleBadResponse() sets error_detail.code to Internal when validation fails, triggering a NACK\\n\\n## Additional Support Components\\n\\n- **GrpcMuxContext** (grpc_mux_context.h) - Configuration context for mux creation\\n- **GrpcMuxFailover** (grpc_mux_failover.h) - Failover support for primary/secondary xDS sources\\n- **EdsResourcesCacheImpl** (eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc) - Caches EDS resources for optimization\\n- **XdsSourceId** (xds_source_id.h/cc) - Tracks xDS source identification\\n- **NewGrpcMuxImpl** (new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc) - Intermediate mux variant for migration\\n\\nThis architecture separates concerns: the GrpcStream handles transport-level gRPC operations, the mux manages resource subscriptions and request queuing, subscription states track protocol state and ACK/NACK logic, and the watch map manages application-level resource interest callbacks.\"\n}\n",
